method based on supramolecular chemistry, widely used for the detection of various analytes. A typical IDA system consists of three core components:\n\n1.  **Host (A):** A molecule possessing a recognition cavity or binding site.\n2.  **Indicator (B):** A guest molecule that exhibits a signal response (e.g., in its color or fluorescence).\n3.  **Analyte (C):** The target guest molecule to be detected.\n\nThe principle of operation involves two steps:\n\n1. If C binds to A more strongly than B does, it will displace the indicator, forming a new complex, `A·C`, and releasing the free indicator B. This displacement restores the indicator's signal to its original state, thus enabling the detection of the analyte C.\n\n------\n\n**Problem Statement**\n\nA given IDA system consists of the following components:\n\n* **Known Component 1:** p-sulfonatocalix[4]arene (SCX4): A water-soluble, anionic host molecule from the calixarene family. A typical IDA system consists of three core components:\n\n1.  **Host (A):** A molecule possessing a recognition cavity or binding site.\n2.  **Indicator (B):** A guest molecule that exhibits a signal response (e.g., in its color or fluorescence).\n3.  **Analyte (C):** The target guest molecule to be detected.\n\nThe principle of operation involves two steps:\n\n1. If C binds to A more strongly than B does, it will displace the indicator, forming a new complex, `A·C`, and releasing the free indicator B. This displacement restores the indicator's signal to its original state, thus enabling the detection of the analyte C.\n\n------\n\n**Problem Statement**\n\nA given IDA system consists of the following components:\n\n* **Known Component 1:** p-sulfonatocalix[4]arene (SCX4): A water-soluble, anionic host molecule from the calixarene family. A typical IDA system consists of three core components:\n\n1.  **Host (A):** A molecule possessing a recognition cavity or binding site.\n2.  **Indicator (B):** A guest molecule that exhibits a signal response (e.g., in its color or fluorescence).\n3.  **Analyte (C):** The target guest molecule to be detected.\n\nThe principle of operation involves two steps:\n\n1. This binding event causes a significant change in the indicator's signal (e.g., fluorescence quenching or a color change).\n2.  When the Analyte (C) is introduced, it competes for the host's cavity. If C binds to A more strongly than B does, it will displace the indicator, forming a new complex, `A·C`, and releasing the free indicator B. This displacement restores the indicator's signal to its original state, thus enabling the detection of the analyte C.\n\n------\n\n**Problem Statement**\n\nA given IDA system consists of the following components:\n\n* **Known Component 1:** p-sulfonatocalix[4]arene (SCX4): A water-soluble, anionic host molecule from the calixarene family. Each phenolic ring is functionalized with a sulfonate group (-SO₃⁻) at the para-position, which imparts high water solubility and creates a negatively charged rim for interacting with cationic guests. A typical IDA system consists of three core components:\n\n1.  **Host (A):** A molecule possessing a recognition cavity or binding site.\n2.  **Indicator (B):** A guest molecule that exhibits a signal response (e.g., in its color or fluorescence).\n3.  **Analyte (C):** The target guest molecule to be detected.\n\nThe principle of operation involves two steps:\n\n1. This binding event causes a significant change in the indicator's signal (e.g., fluorescence quenching or a color change).\n2.  When the Analyte (C) is introduced, it competes for the host's cavity. If C binds to A more strongly than B does, it will displace the indicator, forming a new complex, `A·C`, and releasing the free indicator B. This displacement restores the indicator's signal to its original state, thus enabling the detection of the analyte C.\n\n------\n\n**Problem Statement**\n\nA given IDA system consists of the following components:\n\n* **Known Component 1:** p-sulfonatocalix[4]arene (SCX4): A water-soluble, anionic host molecule from the calixarene family.
